--- Commit Message ---
LU-16064 ldlm: postpone lock cancellation

until all export's RPCs are complete, otherwise lock can be granted to
another client and then RPC processing from just evicted client can
break data consistency.

Signed-off-by: Alex Zhuravlev <bzzz@whamcloud.com>
Change-Id: Id7944cb5583cbe5997e96ee413f7ec70d3faf287

Patch Set 38:

(4 comments)

This is fixing the case of RPCs already in progress in the OSS cache, which is good, because that was submitted before the client was evicted.

Is there (already?) some way to prevent the OST from handling *new* RPCs to this file after the client is evicted?  Otherwise, I'm worried if there is a client sending a lot of cached data that the OSS thread may wait a long time for all of the RPCs to be completed.

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2024-04-30 07:35:51.000000000) ---
Patch Set 39:

> Patch Set 39:
> again. old version had a one lock for very large region, but this may improved to use actual page indexes. and this is don't have an exceptions for MDT - so DoM file corruption isn't protected.

I think this is very local solution for a very specific problem - do not grant locks which are (effectively) used by somebody else.
logically it'd makes sense to have a reference to the lock which is implied, but that would be an extra lookup which is not free.
instead, we can rely on rpc count, which is much cheaper to maintain and check.

--- Message (Vitaly Fertman, 2025-02-24 17:16:26.000000000) ---
Patch Set 49: Code-Review-1

I think we should not postpone all the lock cancelation independently of the ongoing operations. we already check twice if locks exists - before & after IO RPCs on prolong, and we already drop IO which has no locks covering the whole region. it looks better to pin only related locks between those 2 prolong calls.

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2025-02-24 17:25:39.000000000) ---
Patch Set 49:

> Patch Set 49: Code-Review-1
> 
> I think we should not postpone all the lock cancelation independently of the ongoing operations. we already check twice if locks exists - before & after IO RPCs on prolong, and we already drop IO which has no locks covering the whole region. it looks better to pin only related locks between those 2 prolong calls.

I don't think we can really do this - lock pinning != lock grabbing.

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2025-02-24 17:28:20.000000000) ---
Patch Set 49:

> Patch Set 49: Code-Review-1
> 
> I think we should not postpone all the lock cancelation independently of the ongoing operations. we already check twice if locks exists - before & after IO RPCs on prolong, and we already drop IO which has no locks covering the whole region. it looks better to pin only related locks between those 2 prolong calls.

once IO (in ofd) started we don't check locks until the operation is done.

--- Message (Vitaly Fertman, 2025-02-26 20:37:23.000000000) ---
Patch Set 49:

> I don't think we can really do this - lock pinning != lock grabbing.

we can do what is enough to resolve the problem. to grab. or to mark individual locks as not to be cancelled on eviction - so that you know which ones to leave on the export in ldlm_bl_thread_exports.

> once IO (in ofd) started we don't check locks until the operation is done.

we prolong locks twice in advance in ptlrpc_server_request_add() and at the end in ptlrpc_server_finish_request()

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2025-03-27 06:53:57.000000000) ---
Patch Set 49:

> Patch Set 49:
> 
> > I don't think we can really do this - lock pinning != lock grabbing.
> 
> we can do what is enough to resolve the problem. to grab. or to mark individual locks as not to be cancelled on eviction - so that you know which ones to leave on the export in ldlm_bl_thread_exports.

this is what the patch does - do not cancel on eviction and wait for all the export's RPC to complete.
 
> > once IO (in ofd) started we don't check locks until the operation is done.
> 
> we prolong locks twice in advance in ptlrpc_server_request_add() and at the end in ptlrpc_server_finish_request()

we do, but eviction can happen during bulk, for example which may take dozen on seconds and during this time the corresponding thread just sleeps being unable to check/prolong locks.
